ONE. Development with AWS Services

AWS compute services:
- [Instructor] In this lesson, we'll discover the various compute services in AWS. Namely Amazon EC2, AWS Lambda, AWS Elastic Beanstalk, AWS Batch, Amazon LightSail, AWS Outpost, and many more. These can be further classified into four groups, virtual machines, serverless, orchestration, and container services. We'll discuss the first three types in this video. The fourth group, which is the container services, will be presented in the next lesson. All right then, without any further ado, let's begin. If you want to run a Linux or Windows server in AWS, which service should you use? AWS has different competing services that you can choose from. These competing services are basically just servers that allow you to process data or host your applications. AWS owns thousands upon thousands of physical servers that are hosted in numerous data centers around the world. You have the option to either use a dedicated physical server or a virtual machine. AWS uses the process called virtualization to allow a single physical server to run multiple virtual machines that can be ran out by multiple tenants or customers. A virtual machine can be launched and accessed remotely using a web browser, a command line interface, or via an API. These virtual machines are also called instances, which you can customize to meet your technical specifications or resource requirements. You can choose what type of operating system it will run. Including its storage capacity, the number of virtual CPUs, and other available options. You can even choose the type of underlying CPU that will power your instance like Intel, AMT, or Gravitant, which is a new processor designed by AWS. These instances can be reserved for a specific period of time, or availed on a pay-as-you-go basis. There is also an option to choose a non-virtualized environment to run your applications on the physical server used solely by your organization. It allows you to access the hardware features of your underlying server and run your applications with or without a hypervisor. This also allows you to run your own custom virtualization environment and control how instances are placed on a physical server. You can also select a serverless option where you just upload your code or application AWS without having to maintain the server yourself. In this case, server management is entirely handled by AWS. To be clear, serverless competing does not mean no server at all. It still uses service of course, but these competing services are launched, managed, patched, and controlled entirely by the AWS team. AWS even offers a special type of physical server that you can run on your on-premises data center. You can also order storage appliances with competing capabilities to help you expedite your data migration activities. We will now discuss the different competing services available in AWS. Let's start with Amazon Elastic Compute Cloud Service, or Amazon EC2. Amazon EC2 is a computing service that runs virtual servers in the cloud. It allows you to launch Linux or Windows virtual machines to host your application and manage them remotely wherever you are in the globe. Amazon EC2 is categorize as an infrastructure as a service, or IAAS, that acts as a basic building block for your cloud infrastructure. It is also a building block that powers AWS, where it is used by some AWS services as the underlying server for processing, database hosting, and for serverless computing. You and AWS have a shared responsibility in managing your Amazon EC2 virtual machines. AWS manages the data centers, physical facilities, the hardware components, the host operating system, and the virtualization layer that powers the entire Amazon EC2 service. On the other hand, you are responsible for own guest operating system, applying OS patches, setting up security access controls, and managing your data. It is called Elastic Compute Cloud because of its elasticity, or in other words, its ability to be changed, to be resized or to be customized at any given point in time. This provides the flexibility that is not available on traditional physical servers. It can also scale automatically, which means increasing or decreasing the number of running Amazon EC2 instances based on the incoming traffic. The term "C2" in Amazon EC2 just refers to the two C's of the phrase "compute cloud." There are more AWS services and features that you can integrate with Amazon EC2. We'll cover these services in our succeeding lectures. Let's now proceed with AWS Lambda, the other type of compute service in AWS. Lambda is a serverless computing service that allows you to run your code, function, or an entire application without managing any servers. You only pay for the compute time that you actually consumed. Again, serverless computing still uses servers, but all the server management, scaling, and troubleshooting are all done by AWS. An uploaded code in AWS Lambda is also called a Lambda function. These functions can perform a custom task that you can control or program. A Lambda function is also highly scalable. It can instantly support thousands of requests in a matter of seconds. It provides high availability without any additional effort on your part. AWS Lambda is a fully managed service, or in other words, the underlying servers are fully managed by AWS and not you. So unlike Amazon EC2, you can neither access nor manage the underlying server that powers your Lambda function. AWS Lambda supports multiple programming languages such as Java, Go, Ruby, no.js, Python, and many others through the use of runtimes. These runtimes are powered by Amazon Enos EC2, and other servers that are managed by who? Well, you guessed it. Managed by AWS. Again, you can't access these servers directly unlike your Amazon EC2 instance. We will now talk about the AWS services that use Amazon EC2 for its processing. These services don't perform any computing at all. They just orchestrate a group of EC2 instances to perform a specific task. This is different from a serverless computing service like Lambda because you can still access and manage the underlying instances that these services deploy. These orchestration compute services are AWS Batch and AWS Elastic Beanstalk. AWS Batch is a service that enables you to run batch competing workloads on the AWS Cloud. That's why it's called "Batch" in the first place. It dynamically provisions the optimal quantity and type of compute resources based on the volume and specific resource requirements. With AWS Batch, you don't need to install or manage any batch competing software or server clusters to run your jobs. This allows you to focus on analyzing results and solving problems that you're first set out to do. It does the planning, scheduling, and execution of your batch computing workloads using Amazon EC2 instances. AWS Elastic Beanstalk is a service that automates the deployment, management, scaling, and monitoring of your custom applications in AWS. You can just upload your application and Elastic Beanstalk will automatically handle the deployment. From capacity provisioning, load balancing, database management, auto scaling, and even its health monitoring. This service works like the beanstalk in the popular

AWS container services
- [Instructor] AWS provides several container services that allows you to run containerized applications, build microservices, or store your container images. They are the Amazon Elastic Container Service, Amazon Elastic Kubernetes Service, AWS Fargate, and Amazon Elastic Container Registry. AWS also offers tools to easily migrate and manage your containers, such as AWS App2Container, or A2C, and AWS Copilot. First off, let's discuss what a container is and how it is different from a virtual machine. Basically, a virtual machine emulates one or more computers using a single host server. A virtual machine can have the same or different guest operating system than the underlying physical server, which runs the host operating system. A hypervisor is a software that creates and runs virtual machines. On the other hand, a container just emulates an application and not the entire operating system. It is like a lightweight version of a virtual machine without virtualizing each and every hardware components of the host server. A container is commonly used for microservices architecture in which you package an application along with its runtime dependencies. You can either use Docker or Kubernetes in creating your container. Let's now start talking about the different container services in AWS. Amazon Elastic Container Service, or Amazon ECS for short, is a highly scalable, high performance container orchestration service that supports Docker containers. It allows you to easily install, operate, and scale your cluster management infrastructure in AWS. Amazon ECS eliminates the need for you to install and operate your own container orchestration software. It helps you manage the cluster of servers that power your containers. These containers are defined in a task definition, which you use to run individual tasks or are grouped together as a service. You can run your ECS task and services using a serverless compute engine called AWS Fargate, or with Amazon EC2 instances that you can fully access and manage. For security, you can specify an IAM role that can be used by the containers in an ECS task. You can build Docker images and store them in Amazon Elastic Container Registry, or ECR. Just like Amazon EC2, you can integrate Amazon ECS to a wide range of AWS Services. For storage, you can use Amazon EFS or Amazon FSx to store your data. You can design your ECS tasks to talk to each other using an Amazon SQS queue, Amazon Kinesis data stream, or any other integration service. You can also use Amazon ECS Service auto scaling to increase or decrease the number of your ECS tasks automatically. Amazon Elastic Kubernetes Service, or EKS, is a fully managed Kubernetes service. It is portable, accessible, and an open-source platform for managing containerized workloads and services. Kubernetes lets you orchestrate a cluster of virtual machines. Its scheduled containers run on those VMs based on their available resources, and the specified requirements of each container. These containers are grouped into pods. A pod is the basic operational unit in Kubernetes. Amazon EKS allows you to run these pods on either AWS Fargate or Amazon EC2. Unlike Docker, you can easily move and migrate your Kubernetes containers easily since it is not tightly coupled with AWS alone. You can move your containers to your on-premises network, or to other cloud service providers like Microsoft Azure or the Google Cloud platform. This is why Kubernetes is considered as cloud agnostic. AWS Fargate is a serverless compute engine for containers that work with both Amazon ECS and Amazon EKS. Fargate allows you to focus on building your applications without worrying about server provisioning, scaling, and management. It provides a cost effective solution as you only have to pay for the resources required to run your containers. It also avoids over provisioning where you launch a lot of servers that you don't even use in the long run. Fargate runs each ECS task or Kubernetes pod in its own kernel. This provides the tasks and pods in their own isolated compute environment. Amazon Elastic Container Registry, or ECR, is a fully managed Docker container registry that allows you to store, manage, and deploy Docker container images. Amazon ECR is integrated with Amazon ECS to simplify your development to production workflow. It hosts your Docker images in highly available and scalable architecture. This allows you to deploy containers to your apps in a secure and reliable manner. You can also use IAM to provide resource level control of each repository. AWS App2Container, or A2C, is a command line tool for modernizing .NET and Java applications into containerized applications. A2C analyzes and built an inventory of all applications running in virtual machines, on-premises, or in AWS. You just have to choose the application that you want to containerize, and A2C will package the application artifact and dependencies into container images. It also configures the network ports and generates the ECS task and Kubernetes pod definitions. AWS Co-pilot is also a command line interface that enables you to quickly launch and easily manage containerized applications on AWS. Copilot automates each step in the deployment lifecycle of your containers from creating a task definition, creating a container cluster, and pushing the images to a container registry.

AWS database services
- [Instructor] AWS offers a variety of purpose-built databases for all your application needs, from relational, NoSQL, in-memory, data warehouse, and other database types. If you need a relational database, you can use Amazon RDS or Amazon Aurora. These databases have four key properties, atomicity, consistency, isolation, and durability, or ACID for short. These properties guarantee the data integrity of your transactions. Amazon Redshift is also a type of a relational database that is primarily used as a data warehouse. For a non-relational or NoSQL database, you can choose between Amazon DynamoDB or DocumentDB as your data store that provides a flexible schema. For in-memory databases or caching, you can either select Amazon Elastic Cache for Redis or Amazon Elastic Cache for Memcached. AWS offers other databases for specialized workloads as well, namely, Amazon Keyspaces, Amazon Neptune, Amazon Timestream, Amazon QLDB, and many more. Let's first tackle Amazon Relational Database Service, or Amazon RDS. It is quite obvious what this service is for based on its name. Amazon Relational Database Service is a relational database that is managed by both you and AWS. The time-consuming task of hardware provisioning, patching, backups, and maintenance are all handled by AWS. But you also have a certain level of control as well. You can choose and configure the underlying EC2 instance that will be used for your database, from its size storage, instance type, and network access. You also get to decide the actual time when RDS will apply the DB patches in its maintenance window. Amazon RDS makes it easier for you to run various database engines such as Microsoft SQL Server, MySQL, MariaDB, Postgres, Oracle, Aurora, and many others. You can launch your RDS database in a single AZ or in a multi-AZ deployment. In a single AZ, there's only one DB instance deployed within a single availability zone, hence the name single AZ. The instance is called a primary DB instance. For multi-AZ deployments, you have a primary instance in one AZ and another standby instance deployed in a different AZ in the same AWS region. A standby instance is also called a standby replica, since it replicates the data from the primary instance. There is also another type of replica called a read replica that you can use to offload the read request from your primary DB instance. Unlike a standby replica, you can deploy a read replica to a different AWS region. Okay, let's now move on to Amazon Aurora. Amazon Aurora is both a database engine and a fully managed service owned by AWS. Aurora is a relational database that is compatible with both MySQL and Postgres DB engines. This means that your existing code, application, and tools that you're already using with MySQL and Postgres databases can also be used with Aurora, with little or no change. It scales automatically, performs faster, and costs lower than other databases. Amazon Aurora is just like Amazon RDS, but better. It can automatically grow or scale its storage as needed. Aurora is usually deployed as a database cluster. A cluster usually consists of a primary DB instance and multiple Aurora replicas or DB instances. These instances are like the standby or read replicas in Amazon RDS. But instead of calling it Amazon Aurora Multi-AZ Deployments, it is simply called a database cluster. By default, a cluster has a single master configuration, where applications can only write data to a single master DB instance. In a multi-master cluster, all DB instances have read and write capabilities. Amazon RDS and Amazon Aurora are both suitable for applications that read, or write constantly changing data, such as online transaction processing applications, or OLTP. An example of an OLTP application is an e-commerce website that processes thousands of online transactions per hour. Amazon Redshift is a fully managed data warehouse that allows you to analyze all your data using standard SQL, and using your existing business intelligence tools. A data warehouse is just a database optimized to analyze relational data coming from transactional systems, business applications, and other resources. The data stored here has a structure and is optimized for fast SQL queries. This is different from a data lake where the data does not have a structure. Amazon Redshift has a concurrency scaling feature that supports virtually unlimited concurrent users, and concurrent queries to achieve a consistently fast query performance. It also has a feature called Redshift Spectrum that allows you to query and retrieve structured and semi-structured data from files stored in Amazon S3 without having to manually load the data into your Redshift tables. As mentioned earlier, Amazon Redshift is also a relational database like Amazon RDS or Aurora. The main difference is its primary usage. Redshift is mainly used for online analytical processing, or OLAP applications like data reporting and analytics. So, we're through discussing the relational databases in AWS. Let's now talk about the non-relational databases, DynamoDB and DocumentDB. Amazon DynamoDB is a fully managed NoSQL database composed of tables, items, and attributes. The items and attributes in DynamoDB are equivalent to the records and columns in a relational database like Amazon RDS. The term NoSQL is a type of a non-relational database that does not have a rigid schema, or extensive table relationships. In a relational database, a change in just a single column of your table may cause various issues or violations in your table constraints. Two or more tables have a relationship to each other, so any change in the schema or structures of one of the tables can cause a problem. In a NoSQL database like DynamoDB, you can easily add, remove, or modify an attribute without affecting other tables. A DynamoDB table does not have a relationship with other DynamoDB tables. No need to create table joints, foreign keys, or any complex table relationships, so you can safely update your schema at any time. In DynamoDB, you can store complex hierarchical data within a single item and store related items on the same table. Amazon DocumentDB is a fast, scalable, and highly available MongoDB-compatible database service. MongoDB is a document-oriented database program that is cross-platform, and it's also a type of a NoSQL database. In a MongoDB database, you call a table a collection, a row a document, and a column a field. Each document contains fields and values in JSON format with no rigid schema enforced, unlike in traditional SQL databases. This is also the same concept in Amazon DocumentDB. It stores, queries, and index JSON documents. That's how DocumentDB got its name. Let's now discuss in-memory databases in AWS that are primarily used for caching. As its name implies, Amazon Elastic Cache is a caching service that allows you to set up, run, and scale open-source in-memory databases like Memcached or Redis. By storing data in-memory, they can read data more quickly than disk-based databases. If your application experiences performance slowdowns by having frequent calls to return identical datasets, then you must apply database caching to remove this bottleneck. You can refactor your application to use Amazon Elastic Cache and fetch the data in memory instead of phishing the same exact datasets again and again and again. Aside from caching, you can also use this service in real-time analytics, distributed session management, geospatial services, and many more. In Elastic Cache, there are two types of engines that you can launch. These are Amazon Elastic Cache for Memcached, or Amazon Elastic Cache for Redis. Both of these types provide sub-millisecond latency, data partitioning, and require a minimal amount of code to integrate into your application. Amazon ElastiCache for Memcache is based on the open-source Memcached in-memory datastore. This is suitable for building a simple and scalable caching layer for your data-intensive apps. Memcache is multi-threaded, which means that it can utilize multiple processing cores. It helps you handle more operations by scaling up your computing capacity. The downside of using Memcache is its lack of data replication capability that can affect the availability of your cache layer. Amazon Elastic Cache for Redis is based on the open-source Redis in-memory datastore. It provides advanced data structure, pub-sub messaging, geospatial, and point-in-time snapshot support. In addition, it also has a replication feature that is not available in Memcached. So, if you need an in-memory database storage solution that provides high availability using data replication, then this type is the one to use. You just have to enable the cluster mode in Redis to have multiple primary nodes and replicas across two or more availability zones. There are other purpose-built databases in AWS that you can use for specific workloads. Amazon Keyspaces is a scalable, highly available, and managed Apache Cassandra-compatible database service. Apache Cassandra is an open-source, wide-column data store that is designed to handle large amounts of data. With Amazon Keyspaces, you can run Cassandra workloads on AWS without having to provision, patch, or manage servers. Amazon Neptune is a fast, reliable, and fully managed graph database service that makes it easy for you to build and run applications that work with highly connected datasets. It allows you to store billions of relationships and query your data graphs with millisecond latency. Graph databases use nodes to store data entities and edges to store relationships between entities. Amazon Timestream is a fast, scalable, and serverless time series database service for Internet of Things and operational applications. Basically, a time series is a sequence of data points recorded over time interval for measuring events that may have changed at that specific time frame. You can use this to track the changes of stock prices, temperature measurements, and the CPU utilization of an EC2 instance over a specific amount of time. Amazon QLDB is a fully managed ledger database. It provides a transparent and immutable transaction log that is owned by a central trusted authority. These logs are cryptographically verifiable, so you can provide an auditable history of all the changes made to your application data. Amazon QLDB can be used to track each and every application data change.

AWS application integration services
- [Instructor] AWS has a suite of services that you can use to integrate two or more applications. You can also use certain services to automatically notify you of any changes in your systems. These integration services can help you decouple your tightly coupled applications and transform your system into a component-based, service-oriented architecture. By doing so, a failure or a change in one of the components will not affect the entire application, which is a common problem in monolithic architectures. This is perfect for your serverless applications, microservices, and other distributed systems. In this lecture, we will cover the application integration and notification services in AWS. They are Amazon SQS, Amazon SNS, AWS Step Functions, Amazon MQ, Amazon EventBridge, AWS AppSync and Amazon AppFlow. Let us start with Amazon Simple Queue Service, or Amazon SQS. As you might have guessed it, this is primarily used as a queuing service based on its name. It provides a fully managed queue in which the incoming messages can queue, or in other words, the messages can line up one by one, so a consumer in front can process them accordingly. Just like a literal queue. These messages will then be consumed or processed by your EC2 instances, Lambda functions, ECS tasks and other consumers. Amazon SQS can replace your traditional, message-oriented middleware, without having to maintain or manage the underlying resources. It offers two types of message queues, standard queue, and First, in First out queue, or FIFO for short, the standard queue offers an At Least Once delivery with best effort ordering. While the SQS FIFO queue is designed to provide an exactly once delivery. In a FIFO queue, the messages preserve the exact order in which they're sent and received. The standard queue provides higher throughput than FIFO, but it may deliver duplicate messages to your consumers. You can change the visibility timeout of your messages in the queue using the Change Message Visibility API or through your web console. But, this is not a guarantee against receiving a message twice, all the time. On the other hand, the FIFO queue guarantees that all messages will always be delivered exactly once, but with less throughput. This type of queue is perfect for applications where messages must be processed exactly once without any duplicate records and in order in which they're received in the queue. Amazon SQS can also scale your EC2 instances based on the age, depth or number of messages in the queue. It configured an auto-scaling group to scale out your EC2 instances based on the SQS queue depth. You can also configure your Auto-scaling group with a target tracking policy based on the age of the oldest message in the queue. Amazon SQS can be integrated with Amazon SNS, Amazon ECS, and other services to do various functions like getting a notification when a new object is created within your S3 bucket, or sending a message between two ECS microservices and so much more. The Amazon Simple Notification Service, or Amazon SNS, is a fully managed messaging and notification service. Amazon SNS enables you to communicate between systems through publish/subscribe patterns, or pub/sub for short. It enables messaging between decoupled microservice applications or directly to your users via mobile push, email or SMS. It has a resource called a TOPIC. An Amazon SNS TOPIC can be subscribed to by your applications or by other AWS services. For example, Amazon CloudWatch can use an SNS TOPIC to send you an email or a Slack notification for any activities in your auto-scaling group. You can also configure one or more Amazon SQS queues to subscribe to a single SNS TOPIC. Amazon SNS also has a feature called message filtering, where a specific subscriber will only receive a subset of the messages. This can be done by assigning a filter policy to the TOPIC subscription. With message filtering, You can configure one SNS TOPIC to publish specific messages to multiple Amazon SQS queues based on the message type. This is also known as a Fanout Event Notification, where messages are pushed to multiple subscribers, eliminating the need to periodically check or pull the queue for updates. You can use this if you have messages with different types. For example, you can use one SNS TOPIC with a variety of insurance code types, like car insurance, home insurance, or pet insurance code type. For each type, there is one SQS queue that will consume that specific code type. And lastly, you have to configure a backend application server to consume the queue for a particular type. AWS step functions is a serverless function orchestrator for AWS Lambda. What it does is basically allows you to orchestrate or sequence, multiple AWS Lambda functions in order to achieve a specific workflow. In step functions, you can create a state machine using a visual workflow that contains a combination of steps, activities, and service tasks. It helps you coordinate multiple components and configure each and every step in your workflow by using Lambda functions. That's why it's called Step Functions. Amazon MQ is a managed message broker service in AWS that uses the open source Apache Active MQ program. The MQ in Amazon MQ stands for Message Queue, which is a form of a asynchronous communication used in distributed systems, serverless applications or microservices architectures. Messages are stored in the queue until they're processed and deleted by a consumer. It's just like Amazon SQS, but the main difference is the capability of Amazon MQ to support different types of messaging protocols. Amazon MQ provides compatibility with the most common messaging APIs, such as Java Message Service or JMS, .NET Message Service or NMS, AMQP, MQTT, WebSockets and many others. Amazon EventBridge is a serverless event bus that makes it easy for you to connect applications together using data from your own applications, Software-as-a-Service applications, and other AWS services. Under the hood, Amazon EventBridge is a service that is based on CloudWatch events with more advanced features. It actually uses the same service API, endpoint, and the underlying service infrastructure of CloudWatch events. However, Amazon EventBridge is meant to be used for your own applications, third party Software-as-Service apps and other external sources to complement the data provided by AWS services. It is used for building event-driven applications that handle event ingestion, delivery, security, authorization, and error handling for the user. AWS AppSync is a managed service that uses GraphQL to make it easy for applications to get exactly the data they need. GraphQL is a data query language that basically allows you to query your REST APIs exposed as a schema. This schema can be a query schema for reading data, mutation schema for writing data, or a subscription schema for receiving or uploading data. A traditional REST API will return all of the data by default when you call the HTTP GET operation. Most of the time this large amount of data is not even used by your applications. Of course, you can use a curry string parameter to filter your GET operation, but you can only do that for a single resource or in just one schema. You cannot directly use a curry string parameter to combine two or more resources in a single REST API call. It's like downloading 100 items in order to get one item that you actually need. With GraphQL, you can query different APIs or resources easily using a single API call. This enables you to get that one item you need without having to download the entire 100 items that you won't even use. You can query your APIs using a thing called Resolver, which is just a function that resolves or populates the data in your schema. In AWS AppSync, you can easily integrate GraphQL to your applications and easily manage the resolvers and schemas. It simplifies application development by letting you create a flexible API to securely access, manipulate, and combine data from one or more data sources. Amazon AppFlow is a fully managed integration service that enables you to securely transfer data within your Software-as-a-Service applications and different AWS services. It supports different Software-as-a-Service applications such as Salesforce, Marketo, Slack, ServiceNow, and many more. You can also integrate other AWS services like Amazon S3, Amazon Net Shift, and other services in just a few clicks. With AppFlow, you can run your data flows on demand, or by setting up a schedule. You can also run it as a response to a business event. Amazon AppFlow provides you with powerful data transformation capabilities like filtering and validation to easily generate rich and ready to use data for your custom applications.

AWS analytics services
- [Instructor] AWS provides a suite of analytic services that you can use for your unique workloads. These services can be used in big data processing, real-time data analytics, capturing clickstream data from multiple websites, batch processing, near real-time data reporting, Internet of Things, machine learning, data visualization, telemetry, and many other use cases. You can definitely do a lot of things if you have a lot of data. It also empowers you to build your data warehouses and data lakes that your application can use. A data lake is simply a centralized repository that allows you to store all your structured and unstructured data. An unstructured data is simply something that you can directly store as is without having to parse, or structure the data before it can be processed or analyzed. Some of these services are actually using various open-source Apache programs and tools such as Apache Kafka, Apache Spark, Apache Hadoop, Apache Lucene, Apache Flink, Apache Hive, Apache Parquet, Apache Orc, Apache Avro, Apache Oozie, Apache Scoop, Apache HBase, Apache Pig, and many more. You can also see other third-party tools here, such as TensorFlow, Jupyter, Elasticsearch, Presto, etcetera. Expect to see these open-source projects and proprietary tools if you're doing extensive data analytics work in AWS. Performing the data integration process of extract, transform, and load, which is also known as ETL, has become easier and cheaper with serverless AWS services. Developers and data engineers can now visually create, run, and monitor ETL workflows at a fraction of the cost using the different serverless services in AWS. Visualizing your data can be done in a matter of seconds too. The analytic services in AWS are Amazon Kinesis, Amazon Athena, Amazon Elasticsearch Service, Amazon Elastic MapReduce, Amazon QuickSight, Amazon CloudSearch, Amazon Redshift, AWS DataPipeline, AWS Glue, Amazon Managed Streaming for Apache Kafka, AWS Lake Formation, and many more. Okay then, let's now discuss each of these services one by one. We'll first start off with Amazon Kinesis. This service is a suite of services that you can use to analyze data streams in real-time. Yup, you heard that right. You can analyze your data streams in real-time. The data is not just available within seconds, but in a matter of milliseconds. The different Kinesis services allow you to collect, transform, process, load, and analyze the streaming data in real-time, which empowers you to acquire data insights and respond to data changes quickly. Basically, a data stream is a continuous stream, or flow of data. For example, high traffic websites can have a data analytics stream in place that tracks each, and every click on the site to analyze the user's behavior. This type of data stream is called a click stream. And there are many other kinds of data streams that need to be analyzed in real time. The execution of data is done in a short time period, providing near-insustainable output. This enables you to transform, process, and analyze data much faster instead of waiting until all your data is collected before the processing can begin. Amazon Kinesis is comprised of different services, which are Amazon Kinesis Data Streams, Amazon Kinesis Data Firehose, Amazon Kinesis Data Analytics, and Amazon Kinesis Video Streams. Amazon Kinesis Data Streams is a massively scalable and durable real-time data streaming service. It can continuously capture gigabytes of data per second from thousands of sources. The collected data is available in a matter of milliseconds for your real-time data analytics application. This can be used in real-time applications, website click streams, database event streams, Internet of Things telemetry, location tracking events, predictive maintenance, mobile game data streams, online marketplaces with millions of financial transactions, real-time recommendation systems, and many more. It also provides ordering of records, including the ability to read and replay records in the same order to multiple Amazon Kinesis applications. This is suitable if you have a requirement where the data events must be received in an ordered manner or process the mobile game updates in order of receipt. Whenever you see the keywords real-time and maintaining the order of records, then the most likely service that you should use is Amazon Kinesis Data Streams. Multiple applications can consume records from the same Kinesis Data Stream concurrently, while maintaining the order of records based on the time they're added to the stream. It also allows you to consume the records in the same order a few hours later. Amazon Kinesis Data Streams can be used to decouple your architecture. It is somewhat similar to the Amazon Simple Queue service, but with notable differences. Both Kinesis Data Stream and Amazon SQS can accept data from your data sources and forward it to other AWS services for consumption. However, there are certain scenarios where it is better to use Kinesis than SQS. First off, Amazon SQS can't process data in real-time, unlike Kinesis. And second, it doesn't maintain the order of data records by default. Amazon SQS has two types, which are the standard queue and first-in, first-out, or FIFO queue. The former doesn't preserve the exact order in which messages are sent and received, unlike an Amazon Kinesis Data Stream. Nevertheless, a standard SQS queue does provide the highest scalability and throughput. The SQS FIFO queue, on the other hand, maintains the order of records and provides exactly once processing. The issue with this one is its speed and throughput as it only supports a limited number of transactions per second. Again, both of these SQS types don't perform in real-time unlike Kinesis. You can use an Amazon Kinesis Data Stream for various use cases. For example, if you need a solution that captures the clickstream data from multiple websites in real-time, and analyzes it using batch processing, Amazon Kinesis Data Streams enables you to provide near-real-time recommendations for your users. Or for a popular mobile game that streams course updates to a backend system which then posts the results on a leaderboard. Kinesis Data Data Streams can be used to collect the mobile game scores in order of receipt, which can then be processed by an AWS Lambda function. Finally, the processed data can be stored in a highly available database like DynamoDB, which also provides millisecond responsiveness. You can also use this for Internet of Things systems. For example, if you need to implement predictive maintenance on different types of machinery equipments using IoT sensors. These IoT sensors can send data to AWS in real-time, wherein the data stream will receive events in an ordered manner for each machinery asset. Kinesis can also be used as a scalable near real-time solution in processing millions of financial transactions that can be consumed by your internal applications. The records in the data stream can be consumed by Amazon Kinesis Data Analytics, which can be queried by your apps via SQL queries. Let's now discuss the other services in the Amazon Kinesis family. Amazon Kinesis Data Firehose is a fully managed service that provides an easy way to reliably transform, and load your streaming data into data stores and analytics tools. It can deliver data to Amazon S3, Amazon Redshift, Amazon Elasticsearch Service, and any HTTP endpoint. You can also integrate this with your third-party service providers. Kinesis Data Firehose enables your data producers to directly send data to a specific destination, or data store that you specify without having to create custom applications or consumers. You can also configure Kinesis Data Firehose to transform your data before delivering it to the specified destination. Amazon Kinesis Data Stream and Kinesis Data Firehose have a lot of similarities, but they have certain differences too. Both of these services can accept your streaming data in real-time. However, Kinesis Data Stream usually requires an external consumer to store the records into a data store, while Kinesis Data Firehose does not. The primary use case for Kinesis Data Firehose is to act like a hose or a firehose. Imagine that your data is water, and your data producer or data source is the faucet. If you want the water to continuously flow to a different location or to a bucket, then you have to use a hose. In the same way, that's what an Amazon Kinesis Data Firehose is doing. It just delivers your data stream directly to your Amazon S3 buckets, Redshift databases, Amazon ES clusters, and others without the need for a consumer. It can transform the data before it is sent to its destination. This is internally done by invoking a lambda function to transform the incoming source data, and deliver the processed data to its destination. This is recommended if you need to parse the data stream to remove any sensitive data, such as personal data or protected health information. There's also another type of data stream in Kinesis that is used for videos. The Amazon Kinesis Video Streams is a service that securely streams video from connected devices or sources to AWS. This is used for data analytics, machine learning, video playback, and other types of media processing. It automatically provisions and scales all the required infrastructure to ingest streaming video data from millions of devices. An Amazon Kinesis video stream also stores, encrypts, and indexes video data in your streams to improve performance. In addition, it also provides access to your video data through a collection of easy-to-use APIs. The last service for this section is Amazon Kinesis Data Analytics. This is a serverless service that enables you to analyze your streaming data, acquire actionable insights, and respond to events in real-time. The Amazon Kinesis Data Analytics service reduces the complexity of building, managing, and integrating streaming applications with your custom applications and other AWS services. And since it's serverless, it is also cost-effective and highly scalable since you don't have to maintain any servers. Under the hood, it uses Apache Flink to process and analyze streaming data. Apache Flink is an open-source framework that acts as a distributed processing engine for stateful computations over unbounded and bounded data streams. The downside of using Apache Flink is the expensive overhead of setting up, managing, and maintaining your own server. Kinesis Data Analytics also enables you to author and run code against streaming sources to provide real-time dashboards, perform time series analytics, and create real-time metrics. With this, the data can be analyzed using SQL queries, and the results can be delivered to Amazon S3, Amazon Redshift, and other data stores using Kinesis Data Firehose. You can use Java or Scala to process and analyze your streaming data. Amazon Kinesis Data Analytics can be used in various ways, such as in near real-time data processing and data querying for acquiring timely insights of your application, for processing your streaming data with minimal effort and operational overhead, for providing scalable and near real-time data querying with minimal data loss, and many more. You can also integrate this with other AWS services. For example, you can analyze the location data points of your GPS application that tracks the movement of people, bikes, automobiles, or any other moving object. The Amazon Kinesis Data Stream can send the streaming data to Kinesis Data Analytics for running near real-time queries. You can also set up a REST API in API Gateway that can be used as an Amazon Kinesis proxy to allow access to your data points. Now that we are through discussing the different types of Amazon Kinesis services, let's continue to explore the different data analytics services in AWS. Amazon Athena is an interactive query service for your data that is stored in Amazon S3. It simplifies data analysis in Amazon S3 using standard SQL. You can also query a subset of S3 data using Amazon S3 Select via simple SQL statements. But this is quite limited. Athena is more powerful than S3 Select as it can query your entire S3 data lake and not just its subset. Athena is serverless too, so you only pay for the specific queries that you run. Say, for example, a global e-commerce website stores 250GB of transactional data each month in Amazon S3. If you need to identify the number of items sold in each particular region for the previous month in the most cost-effective way, then you can use Amazon Athena. You can also use Amazon Redshift, Amazon EMR, or an Amazon ES cluster to fulfill these requirements. But these services are not serverless, so using them may entail a high operating cost, unlike Athena. You can also integrate it with other AWS services. Athena can use an AWS Glue data catalog to store and retrieve table metadata for your Amazon S3 data and provide data visualization using Amazon QuickSight. The Amazon Elasticsearch service is a fully managed Elasticsearch service. As its name implies, Elasticsearch is a search engine that is based on the Apache Lucene library. Elasticsearch is a distributed, multi-tenant-capable, full-text search engine with an HTTP web interface that can store data as a schema-less JSON document. So essentially, the Amazon Elasticsearch service just abstracts this underlying technology, provisions the necessary infrastructure, and automatically manages the resources so you don't manually do it yourself. It also allows you to launch an ELK stack in AWS. An ELK stack is simply a collection of three open source products, namely Elasticsearch, Logstash, and Kibana. Logstash is a server-side data processing pipeline, while Kibana is simply a user interface that lets you visualize your Elasticsearch data. The service provides support for open-source Elasticsearch APIs, Managed Kibana, integration with Logstash, and other AWS services. Amazon Elasticsearch service lets you pay only for what you use, meaning there are no upfront costs or usage requirements. Let's now discuss Amazon Elastic MapReduce, which is also called Amazon EMR. This service allows you to run different types of big data frameworks in AWS. This is a managed big data platform for processing vast amounts of data using open source tools, such as Apache Hadoop, Flink, HBase, HCatalog, Hive, Hudi, Hue, Jupyter, Levy, MXNet, Oozie, Phoenix, Pig, Presto, Spark, Scoop, TensorFlow, Tex, Zeppelin, Zookeeper, and many more. It is quite obvious that you can run a lot of open source data analytics workloads with Amazon EMR. Technically, Amazon EMR runs your big data framework on Amazon EC2 instances, Amazon Elastic Kubernetes Service clusters, or in your on-premises EMR cluster via AWS Outposts. These compute resources are deployed in your VPC and then group as an Amazon EMR cluster. You can directly access and control the underlying EC2 instances of your EMR cluster. Take note that this service is not serverless since it is using Amazon EC2 and EKS. The Amazon EMR service just automates the server provisioning and management process for you. The data in your EMR cluster can also interact with other AWS data stores, such as Amazon S3 and Amazon DynamoDB. Amazon QuickSight is a scalable, serverless, embeddable, machine learning-powered business intelligence service. It lets you create and publish interactive dashboards that can be accessed from different browsers or mobile devices. You can also embed dashboards in your applications. Amazon QuickSight is highly scalable and can easily scale up to thousands of users without any software to install, servers to deploy, or infrastructure to manage. Amazon Cloud Search is a managed search service in AWS. This is helpful if you want to implement a search feature in your application. For example, you can use this to retrieve contents of selected fields, for providing facet information that enables you to categorize the results, statistics for the values contained in numeric fields, highlights that shows the search hits in the field data, auto-complete suggestions, geospatial search, and many more. It allows you to create a search domain, specify an index, and upload your data as documents. Cloud Search provisions and manage all the underlying servers, and resources needed to build and deploy search indexes. All you have to do is upload your data to a search domain and integrate it into your applications. This next service that we will tackle is both a database service, and an analytic service in AWS. Amazon Redshift is a fast, scalable data warehouse that allows you to analyze all your data across your data warehouse and data lake. It delivers 10 times faster performance than other data warehouses through the use of machine learning, massively parallel query execution, and columnar storage on high-performance disks. You can run queries across petabytes of data in your Redshift data warehouse, and analyze exabytes of data in your Amazon S3 data lake. This is primarily used for online analytical processing or OLAP applications and reporting tools. Amazon Redshift clusters run in internal Amazon EC2 instances that are configured as nodes. You can select a particular node type and instance size that you select. Since it uses Amazon EC2 to run, Redshift is not a serverless service, so you have to be wary of its associated costs. It also has a feature called Redshift Spectrum that allows you to query data from Amazon S3 without loading the entire data to Redshift tables. Redshift Spectrum queries use massive parallelism to quickly execute large datasets at a fraction of the cost. AWS Data Pipeline is a service that processes, and moves your data between different AWS compute and storage services. You can process and move your data in specific intervals that you define, as well as transfer data to and from your on-premises data center. It allows you to regularly access your data where it's stored, transform it to a specified format, and process it at scale. You can also transfer and store the results to various AWS services, such as Amazon S3, Amazon RDS, Amazon DynamoDB, and Amazon EMR. AWS Glue is simply a fully managed and serverless service that is primarily used to extract, transform, and load workloads or ETL. It simplifies the process of preparing and loading your data before running your data analytics workload. In AWS Glue, you can create a data catalog that allows you to specify and search your data that is stored on Amazon S3 and other AWS services. AWS Glue can automatically discover your data and store the associated metadata in the AWS Glue data catalog. Your data will be immediately searchable, queryable, and available for ETL once the metadata is stored. Amazon Managed Streaming for Apache Kafka is a fully managed Apache Kafka service in AWS. Apache Kafka is an open source platform that allows you to build real-time streaming data pipelines and applications. With this service, you can use Apache Kafka APIs to stream changes to and from different databases, populate your Amazon S3 data lakes, and empower machine learning and analytics applications. And finally, let's end this lecture by discussing the AWS Lake Formation service. As its title suggests, this one makes it easy for you to set up a secure data lake. Just as I mentioned at the beginning of this lesson, a data lake is simply a centralized, curated, and secure repository that stores all your data that can be structured or in its raw form. Like AWS Glue, the AWS Lake Formation Service also allows you to create data catalogs for your external data. It collects and catalogs your data from different data sources and moves the data into your new Amazon S3 data lake. It also classifies and processes your data using machine learning algorithms, and secures access to your sensitive data. The data can be queried and analyzed using Amazon Athena, Amazon Redshift, Amazon EMR, and other services.

AWS storage services
- [Instructor] AWS offers a complete range of storage services that you can use for your cloud infrastructure. These services enable you to store, access, control, and analyze your data to help you reduce your costs and improve your storage systems. You can use virus AWS storage services for storing different types of data, such as block storage, object storage, file storage, and many others. There are also services available to store your backups and integrating AWS with their on-premises storage appliances. In this lecture, we'll talk about Amazon EC2 Instance Store, Amazon Elastic Block Store, Amazon Simple Storage Service, Amazon S3 Glacier, Amazon Elastic File System, Amazon FSx for Lustre, Amazon FSx for Windows Server, AWS Backup, and AWS Storage Gateway. We will discuss the primary functions of these storage services one by one. We will also cover the type of data that you should store for each of these services. Let's begin with the two types of block storage in AWS, the Amazon EC2 Instance Store and the Amazon Elastic Block Store, or Amazon EBS. The Amazon EC2 Instance Store provides a temporary block level storage for your Amazon EC2 instance. An in instant store is ideal for ephemeral or temporary data storage. It's basically using the disks that are physically attached to the underlying host computer where your EC2 instance is running. Remember that AWS has thousands of data centers around the world. And in each data center, they have hundreds of thousands of physical server racks. One server can run a hypervisor that generates thousands of Amazon EC2 instances. That server and the actual storage device that powers the EC2 instance store are physically connected under one server rack. In reality, an instance store can be a hard disk drive with actual disk on it or a non-volatile memory express solid state drive, which is just a chip. Because the storage device is literally attached to EC2, it provides low latency access to the data. Unlike a network-based file system, you can also use this to store temporary buffers, caches, or scratch data. It works like a random access memory or RAM that loses its stored data when the computer is shut down, so you have to keep in mind that your data will be deleted when your EC2 instance is either stopped or terminated. This is suitable if your data is replicated across a fleet of Amazon EC2 instances or a load balance pool of web servers. Amazon Elastic Block Store or Amazon EBS is a persistent block level storage service, primarily used for your Amazon EC2 instances. As its name implies, it's also a block storage service like the Amazon EC2 Instance Store. The main difference is the data persistence. The data in EBS does not get lost easily. You can stop, restart, and terminate your instance and your files will still be there. These block storages are also called the EBS volumes, which you can mount or attach to your EC2 instances and EBS volume is zonal in scope, which means you can only attach a volume to any EC2 instances in the same availability zone. Your data can also be encrypted at rest using the AWS Key Management Service or KMS. Amazon EBS or its two kinds of volume, solid state drive or hard disk drive. A solid state drive or SSD performs faster than a hard disk drive or HDD, and it is suitable for workloads with frequent read/write operations. SSDs provides a high input/output operations per second performance or IOPS. On the other hand, HDDs offers a high megabit per second performance or also known as throughput. This is actually similar to the SSDs or HDDs that you have on your computer. Modern laptops today like MacBook, Microsoft Surface, and other new computers are only using SSDs. That's why the boot of time for these computers is lighting fast. In the contrary, the old computers with HDDs are often slow. If you have an external hard drive where you store your old backup files, that device is basically a hard disk drive. In Amazon EBS, there are four types of volumes. General purpose, provision IOPS, throughput optimized, and called HDD. The first two types are SSD based, while the other two are HDDs. And EBS volume is usually attached to just one EC2 instance. Amazon EBS also provides low latency access to your data. You can retrieve your files faster if it is stored in an SSD-based EBS volume instead of Amazon S3 or Amazon EFS. You can also use an SSD as the boot volume for your EC2 instance, which is not supported by HDDs. There's also a feature called EBS multi-attach that allows you to attach two or more provisioned IOPS EBS volumes to a single EC2 instance. Take note that this feature is not supported on all volume types, but only to provisioned IOPS volumes. You can only use micro based EC2 instances in order to use this EBS multi attached feature. Other types of EC2 instances are not supported. It is also important to know that although multiple EC2 instances can use the same provision IOPS EBS volume, these instances cannot concurrently modify or access the same file at exactly the same time. If you need this functionality, you have to use the Amazon EFS file system instead. Amazon Simple Storage Service or Amazon S3 is an object storage service in AWS. It is a highly durable and scalable service with many available features that you can use. You can store virtually a limited amount of data to a resource called an Amazon S3 bucket. The files that you upload in this bucket are considered as are objects. You can store large amounts of files, documents, videos, database backups and snapshots, and many other data in an S3 bucket that you own or own by others. Accessing objects from an S3 bucket is done by a REST API call. There are different storage classes that you can choose in Amazon S3 to place your objects. You can use the S3 Standard Storage class to store your frequently accessed data. The S3 Intelligent-Tiering class for storing data with changing or unknown access patterns. S3 Standard infrequent Access and S3 One Zone-Infrequent Access for storing long live, yet less frequently accessed data. And for low cost long-term storage and data archiving, you can use Amazon S3 Glacier or Amazon S3 Glacier Deep Archive. It also has a feature called Lifecycle Policy that automatically transitions or moves your data from one storage class to another. Amazon S3 also offers security, versioning, and replication capabilities to manage your objects effectively. You can use the Amazon S3 Access Control List to secure access to your S3 buckets and objects. You can also create an S3 bucket policy for controlling external access to your bucket. S3 versioning and multi-factor authentication are the features that you can enable to prevent accidental data deletion in S3. Your objects can be replicated to a different AWS region using the cross region and replication feature or CRR. Data transfer can be expedited by using the Amazon S3 transfer acceleration and the S3 multi-part upload option. The next service that we'll cover is Amazon S3 Glacier. This is actually one of the storage classes in Amazon S3, but it has a web console of its own in a different set of APIs apart from Amazon S3. Historically, Amazon S3 Glacier is just called Amazon Glacier before and it's totally separate from S3. These two storage services were eventually merged into one. The name of the service is based on the word glacier, a cold, large mass of ice. If your data is really accessed, it is considered as cold data. And if it is frequently accessed, it's referred to as hot data. This is also the same concept with cold HDD volumes in Amazon EBS. Amazon S3 data share provides low cost storage for data archiving and long-term backup. This is suitable for files that are rarely accessed in archive for a number of years to meet your regulatory requirements. The archive files are stored in a resource called the vaults. You can further lower down your storage costs by using the Amazon S3 Glacier Deep Archive class, which is the cheapest storage type in AWS if you're archiving rarely access data for seven to 10 years. There is an additional fee if you want to retrieve your Glacier data immediately. Again, the storage glass is only the cheapest type if you're only archiving your data for a lot of years and not for a few hours or a couple of days. Remember that the objects archive in the S3 Glacier and S3 Glacier Deep Archive have a minimum storage duration of 90 days and 180 days respectively. Objects deleted before that period incur a prorated charge equal to the storage charge for the remaining days. So if you store data in Glacier for only 24 hours and then you deleted it, you'll have to pay the storage charge for the hole 90 days and not just for the one day of storage. Same goes for Glacier Deep Archive. Once you stored and deleted your objects within a day, you'll have to pay the storage charge for the hole 180 days. In this case, it's way cheaper to store your temporary data in the S3 Standard class than in Glacier. The disadvantage of using Glacier is the time it takes to retrieve your archive data. Just like frozen meat that you have to thaw, you also have to wait for a while in order for a data in Glacier to become available. Amazon Glacier offers three types of archive retrieval options. These are expedited, standard, and bulk. Amazon Elastic File System or Amazon EFS is a scalable shared file storage solution. It provides a process compliant shared file system that can be simultaneously accessed by multiple Amazon Linux EC2 instances in different availability zones. Amazon EFS is using the Network File System protocol or NFS and as such, you have to mount the EFS file system to Linux EC2 instances or to your on-premises servers, just like a regular network file share. Amazon EFS only supports Linux servers and can't be used by Windows base EC2instances. If you need a shared Windows file system, you have to use the Amazon FSx for Windows server instead. In Amazon EFS, you can choose between a standard or an infrequent access storage class. The standard storage class is best for active file system workloads, while the latter is a cheaper storage class that's cost optimized for infrequently accessed files. Similar to Amazon S3, you can also use a lifecycle policy to automatically move your data from the standard class to the infrequent access storage class. Let's now move on to the two types of Amazon FSx services. FSx for Lustre and FSX for Windows Server. Amazon FSx for Lustre is quite similar to Amazon EFS. It's also a process compliant shared file system that only supports Linux servers. The word Lustre actually refers to the open source file system that the service is using. Lustre is a parallel file system used for large scale cluster computing. The name Lustre is basically a combination of the word Linux and cluster. FSx for Lustre is primarily used for high performance computing, machine learning and HPC applications that needs high performance parallel storage for frequently access hot data. This service can provide a throughput of hundreds of gigabytes per second and millions of IOPS to support your demanding workloads. You can mount an Amazon FSx for Lustre file share to your EC2 instances or your containers. You can use the Container Storage Interface or CSI to connect your Amazon EKS cluster. Amazon FSx for Windows Server is essentially just a fully managed Microsoft Windows file server. Unlike cluster, which is Linux based, this service is backed by a fully native Windows file system. There are a lot of Microsoft-based technologies that you can integrate with this service. You can ask this file share using the server message block protocol or SMB. SMB is a protocol commonly used by Windows Servers. You can also integrate your existing Microsoft Active Directory supervision file system access to your users. The Amazon FSx for Windows Server can be used as a shared file storage for your Microsoft SharePoint, Microsoft SQL server database, Windows container, or any other Windows-based applications. Moving on, let's talk about AWS backup. The function of this service is quite obvious based on its name. AWS backup is a fully managed backup service that makes it easy to automate your server and database backups. By default, the automated backups of your RDS databases only have a seven-day retention period. The maximum retention period is 35 days. By using AWS backup, you can perform a daily snapshot of your database with a retention set to 90 days, a year, or even longer. You can also create a lifecycle policy to automatically move your backups to cold storage. And last but not least, it's now discussed the AWS Storage Gateway. AWS Storage Gateway is a hybrid cloud storage service that connects your on-premises data storage to the AWS Cloud. It allows your on-premises application to seamlessly use cloud storage services available in AWS. It is mainly used to integrate your local and cloud storage systems by using a gateway. A gateway is just a virtual machine or a hardware appliance running on your on-premises data center. This service has three types, file gateway, volume gateway, and a tape gateway. A file gateway provides the ability for you to store and retrieve objects in Amazon S3 using the NFS and SMB protocols. File gateway can also work with your Microsoft Active Directory, either hosted on premises or in AWS. You can also access your data using S3 APIs. If you don't have a virtualized computer sources, you can also use a hardware appliance hosted on premises to replicate your local data to Amazon S3. The second type is volume gateway. This type provides block storage to your on-premises application via the internet small computer system interface or iSCSI. It also uses Amazon S3 to store your data by taking point in time snapshots of your volumes. This allows you to generate Amazon EBS snapshots that you can use for your EC2 instances. A volume gateway can run in either a cache or stored mode. Cache volumes store the primary data in Amazon S3 while retaining copies of the frequently accessed data subsets locally. Stored volumes on the other hand still store the entire dataset on premises and just asynchronously backup up the data to AWS. The third type is the tape gateway. This is essentially a cloud-based virtual tape library or VTL. Just like file gateway in volume gateway, this one also uses Amazon S3. You also have the option to store the archive tapes in Amazon S3 Glacier or Amazon S3 Glacier Deep Archive. Your on-premises backup application can connect your tape gateway as an iSCSI devices. It helps you reduce the cost of eliminating the use of physical backup tapes while preserving the existing investment of your on-premises backup applications and workflows. Storage gateway is suitable for building a hybrid cloud storage infrastructure where your on-premises storage systems are actively sending data to AWS. If you're planning to totally immigrate your data to the cloud and decommission your on-premises storage, then it is better to use the AWS DataSync service instead.

AWS monitoring services
- Monitoring is a vital process in managing your modern IT infrastructure. It provides visibility on how your systems are doing and helps you forecast performance issues based on the current state of your services. It can help you detect issues on your systems and assist you in troubleshooting errors. You can use certain AWS services to monitor the health of other AWS services that your applications are using. These monitoring services can check the CPU utilization, disk usage, network performance, and other system metrics. You can also track the logs of your applications easily instead of manually logging into the server and checking the logs yourself. In this lecture, we'll discuss Amazon CloudWatch, AWS Service Health Dashboard, AWS Personal Health Dashboard, and AWS Health API. Amazon CloudWatch is a suite of AWS services used in monitoring your systems on both AWS, as well as in your on-premises network. CloudWatch is basically a metrics repository that collects systems data from AWS services and the custom metrics that you publish. It monitors and analyzes these metrics and notifies you if a certain threshold has been reached. You also have the option to trigger a certain action based on a specific threshold or events that you define. Amazon CloudWatch has several related services that you can choose from. They are CloudWatch Metrics, CloudWatch Logs, CloudWatch Alarms, CloudWatch Events, CloudWatch Dashboards, and many more. The primary task of the CloudWatch Metrics service is to collect the metrics from the AWS services and your custom applications. You can also aggregate the metrics across multiple resources. Most AWS services send metric data to CloudWatch every one minute by default. However, for Amazon EC2, the metrics are only sent every five minutes. You can enable the Detailed Monitoring feature in Amazon EC2 to view the metrics in a one-minute period. CloudWatch Logs is a monitoring service for your logs. It allows you to monitor, store, and access your log files generated from your AWS services or your custom applications. With this service, you can easily analyze, monitor, or even query your log data from various AWS resources and services. You can also do the same thing for your custom applications. Just install a CloudWatch Logs agent to your EC2 instances, and it will automatically collect and publish your application logs to CloudWatch. CloudWatch Alarms is another service in the CloudWatch family. As its name implies, it is primarily used for setting alarms as part of your monitoring process. You can create a CloudWatch alarm that performs one or more actions based on a system metric and a specific threshold. So if a metric reaches the threshold that you define, the alarm will be triggered and it'll notify you using Amazon SNS. You can also trigger a custom action, too, like auto-scaling your EC2 instances, sending a billing alert, or invoking a Lambda function. CloudWatch Events is a service that monitors and responds to the system events of your AWS services in near real-time. You can create a CloudWatch Event rule to track the changes or the state of your services and do a particular action. If a certain event occurred and it matches your event rule, the action that you specified will be invoked. You can also use this for a scheduled job that regularly runs for a period of time. For example, you can create a scheduled job using a CloudWatch Events rule that invokes a Lambda function on a regular basis, like every hour, every day, every week, or any schedule that you like. A CloudWatch Dashboard is just a customizable dashboard in the CloudWatch web console. You can use this board to monitor your resources in a single view, even if those resources are located across different AWS Regions. You can also publish and view your custom metrics using the CloudWatch Dashboards. And that's a wrap for the different services in the Amazon CloudWatch family. Let's now move on to the AWS Service Health Dashboard. This is basically just a public dashboard that shows the status of all AWS services across the various regions. The AWS Service Health Dashboard contains the most up-to-the-minute information on the service availability of each and every AWS service. You can be notified of any service interruptions by subscribing to an RSS feed. AWS Personal Health Dashboard provides a personalized dashboard that shows the status of the AWS services that you are using. Unlike the Service Health Dashboard, it won't show you the status of all the AWS services. You can only view the services that you're actually using in your account. It also shows the AWS Health events that might affect your applications running on AWS. These events could be a scheduled maintenance of the underlying hardware or infrastructure used by AWS to render cloud services. You can create alerts and notifications triggered by the changes in the health of your AWS resources. This provides you with a bird's eye view of your AWS services and helps you troubleshoot your systems faster. AWS Health API provides programmatic access to the AWS Health information that appears in your AWS Personal Health Dashboard. The AWS Health API is basically a RESTful web service that you can access via HTTPS and return your response in JSON format. This service is not available by default. You must have a Business or Enterprise support plan in order for you to use the service.

AWS networking and content delivery services
- [Instructor] In this lesson, we will briefly go through the different networking and content delivery services in AWS. These networking services are used to enable communication between multiple AWS components to optimize your application performance. AWS offers various tools and services to deliver your content securely and with low latency anywhere in the world. These services also helps you to integrate your on-premises data center or any external network to your AWS Cloud infrastructure. We'll discuss Amazon VPC, elastic load balancing, Amazon Route 53, AWS Global Accelerator, Amazon CloudFront, AWS PrivateLink, AWS Virtual Private Network, AWS Direct Connect, AWS Transit Gateway, Amazon API Gateway, AWS App Mesh, and AWS Cloud Map. The Amazon Virtual Private Cloud, or Amazon VPC is a logical private network within the AWS Cloud. It allows you to launch Amazon EC2 instances and other resources in the virtual network that you define. You have complete control over your virtual networking environment from selecting your IP address range, creating subnets, route table configuration, and adding gateways for your external networks. You can use both IP version 4 and IP version 6 addresses in your VPC for your cloud resources and applications. A VPC can communicate to external networks using a gateway. Just like a regular gate, a gateway provides a way for the traffic to go into your virtual network or go out to the public internet, to your on-premises network, or to other external networks. An internet gateway provides internet connectivity to your VPC, while a virtual private gateway allows you to connect to an on-premises data center or to external networks. You can also connect to another VPC using a feature called VPC peering. Obviously, the term VPC is the acronym for Virtual Private Cloud. These three words can give you an idea of what it really is. For the first one, the word virtual means that this thing is a virtual entity that is powered by a group of interconnected physical networking devices. A network device can be a router, a switch, or a network interface card. Just as a hypervisor instantiates a virtual machine, so does this collection of network devices creates a virtual private cloud. These network adapters or network controllers allow communications between multiple hardware servers across different data centers. This thing is generated by a physical networking device. This network device is basically just a network interface card, which is also known as a network adapter or network controller. Somewhere in one of the data centers of AWS, there's a hardware server rack with a PCIe express attached network interface card, and this physical device is what creates a VPC. This is the basics of the underlying physical components of an Amazon VPC. For the second word, it means that a VPC is a private network. If you create a new VPC, then by default, it is totally private. It does not have any gateway to other external networks. No other entity or person can access it. You won't be able to access this over the public internet unless you add an internet gateway to your VPC. That is how private a virtual private cloud is. An AWS Outpost rack also has the same physical networking devices used by AWS on their data centers. This allows you to create subnets and extend your Amazon VPC to your on-premises data center. By using AWS Outpost, you can extend your regular VPCs into AWS Cloud to your regional VPCs hosted locally. Lastly, the word cloud essentially means that you don't have to manage physical servers yourself. Cloud computing is an on-demand delivery of compute power, database storage, applications, and other IdP resources via the Internet with pay-as-you-go pricing. Your virtual machines like EC2 instances are usually launched within your VPC. You can also establish a private connection between your VPC and some AWS services using a VPC endpoint. Since the connection is private, the traffic does not traverse the public internet. Elastic Load Balancing or ELB is a networking service that automatically distributes incoming traffic across multiple targets, such as Amazon EC2 instances, containers, lambda functions, and other components. As its name implies, this service is primarily used in load balancing, or in other words, distributing the incoming traffic load to multiple underlying servers. So instead of just having a single server to process the load, you can launch multiple servers to handle the application request and to provide high availability. With an ELB, you can route the traffic to healthy resources running in different availability zones. There are different types of elastic load balancers that you can use, namely application load balancer or ALB, network load balancer or NLB, gateway load balancer or GWLB, and classic load balancer or CLB. An ALB is suitable for load balancing HTTP and HTTPS traffic to your application servers, microservices and containers. NLB is recommended for load balancing TCP, UDP, and TLS traffic to your applications. It can also handle millions of requests per second while maintaining ultra-low latencies. GWLB is primarily used for deploying, scaling, and running third-party virtual appliances. These virtual appliances can be your own custom firewalls, deep packet inspection systems, or intrusion detection and prevention systems in AWS. A gateway load balancer is mainly using the internet protocol or IP to pass the OSI layer 3 traffic to its registered targets. Finally, CLB is intended for applications that were built within the old EC2-classic network. It is still being used today for applications with custom security policies and TCP passthrough configuration. Amazon Route 53 is a domain name system web service that routes traffic to various targets. A domain name system or DNS is basically just a system that routes a domain name to a particular IP address. Route 53 allows you to map domain names to your elastic IP addresses, EC2 instances, static S3 websites, elastic load balancer, CloudFront distributions, and other AWS resources. It also allows you to purchase and manage your custom web domains. So if you have a website called tutorialsdojo.com, you can route the traffic to an EC2 server, an S3 static website, a load balancer, or any AWS resource that you prefer. You can also use a route policy that allows you to customize how the traffic is routed to a specific domain. There are different route policies that you can choose, namely simple, failover, geolocation, geoproximity, latency, multivalue answer, or weighted routing policy. AWS Global Accelerator is a networking service that provides a set of static IP addresses that serves as a single fixed entry points for your clients around the world. You can associate these static IP addresses to regional endpoints, such as network load balancers, application load balancers, EC2 instances, or elastic IP addresses. With global accelerator, you can connect multiple AWS resources that are running in one or more AWS regions using a single endpoint or an endpoint group. The static IP addresses accepts incoming traffic onto the AWS global network that is in close proximity to your users.
